Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	In various ways, abscesses come in the anus, such as boils, pierced abscesses, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and other diseases that I have said before. Therefore, it is necessary for me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the anus, which is not the same as those that close with a bowel; and if you want to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is acute at the beginning of its appearance, filled with heat and fever, and turns red if it can be seen. Do not hurry to pierce, but let it heal until the pain subsides; then make the patient sit on one seat, and provide two seats for him or her to lean against, support his back and spread his legs apart at the knees; and have his thighs open, place his arms beneath his thighs, and bind them well with a strong cord; then press the pus towards the right side of the body, and bring the instrument that opens the anus; the shape follows from here. It is necessary that when you bring this instrument, you pierce first to know the depth of the anus so that what enters does not go further than it should, and does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the anus with cloths so that the instrument does not hurt. It must be placed above, and marked. When the abscess opens and becomes soft, it must be covered with a linen gauze, or with a green dry oil; and place the gauze over the opening and over the handle clean linen moistened in vinegar or boiled herbs such as long-roots or Aristolochia. Then apply ointment for two days following this procedure, until it is healed; sometimes the anus and the wound are lifted with oil and honey enema, and then with cooked vinegar or long-root herbs and Aristolochia; return to the ointment afterward. If the wound returns in the anus, it is necessary to be careful of iron, but treat it as we have said before.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the figure of natural childbirth and the signs when you see the woman urging downward, desiring to smell the anus; then hasten the infant to be born; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and it comes out with its head, and follows with the second one; and when you see these signs, gently press her belly so that the infant is born quickly; for when it descends upon its head, it is followed by the other, and the husband sheds his waste through good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For at times, it comes above the feet, and the body or the shoulders, or the hands, or above the belly, or the backside, and is turned accidentally on its neck, and by other evil figures; it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skillful in these matters, and to avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures as to how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes out upon its head by natural childbirth, and the woman labors painfully, and her strength is weak, let her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; then anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then insert the small spatula between her legs in the form shown:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And cut open the second birth canal, and hit its fingernail to expel the afterbirth which is inside; and grab the woman's stomach until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must plaster her with musk-infused fenugreek oil; then make her grasp and vomit of contraction, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour; thus the child will be born now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes out on its feet, you must push it upwards.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it gradually, until it is even;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one piece and stretch it gradually.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	If he is able to jump up to his knees, when commanded, and makes him vomit with discomfort;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it can be done, God willing.   Here the author suggests that a patient who is able to jump up to their knees when commanded, and then vomits from discomfort, may have a fracture in the lower part of the leg or thigh bone. The text does not elaborate on how this could be determined, but the idea is that these symptoms could potentially indicate the presence of a fracture.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it bit by bit until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it will be easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	If it does not come as we have said, take musk-mallow of high quality, oil of sage, and melted gum, and grind all in one mortar.
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and spread it on the woman's nature (or body) outside this ointment,   --> and apply this ointment to the woman's body from the outside
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	Then make him sit upright in acute agony until below the ribs.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	And when it is softened beneath, make one myrrh cataplasm and put it beneath, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then make him sit on a chair, then make him vomit and hold his mouth and nose shut, and lightly press his stomach because he is farting now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's excrement over its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When a child comes in this form, put the poultice on its hands little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	and be careful on its neck, let the feet hang downwards, and lie it on one bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	fold its hands little by little, and then bind its hands above the stomach, and unfasten the cushions beneath until it is prepared below;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	if the child does not jump, take its feet and bend them upwards, then bend the stomach above, and put your hands there;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And rock the child gently, and instruct the woman to take hold of herself until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the delivery of the child that comes forth with one hand wide.
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to use a device for pulling back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be pulled back, make her get up and walk.   --> If the child cannot come out naturally, the woman should rise and walk.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If it cannot walk, lay it on a bed or a flat surface, and bend its legs.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the musk-like substance as I have mentioned.
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if it does not give birth, lay it on a chair, then study how to bring back the hand.
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and help the child according to its natural shape, make it vomit, and command it to hold on until the afterbirth is expelled.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the birth of the child on its neck, and if it has spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	The servant should touch the baby's hand, then turn it gently and easily.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	And when it is even, put some muscle-relaxant of alum and oil, as we have said, then command it to move gently.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	And when you have done this, make her sit on a chair or seat, and command her to take hold of it; then make her vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way, support her all the second time.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to be in this manner all the second time, if you press the second time with your nail, until the moisture is voided;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	If the intestines push up against its place and on its neck, if you press from the bottom, so that it is not retained, and the intestine dies.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then push the child inside as much as you have placed it correctly, and command the woman to take herself once:
adonques si istra legierement.	Then gently ease it out.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is known that twins are born frequently and sometimes even four; and this is not strange and does not happen rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are strange things, and do not live unless called by name;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know these, that they are multiply and desire the one who creates them, which is bound to the earth;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come out naturally like a child born, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if it [the dislocation] occurs with a loud noise, then follow the cure as we have said, and let the balm be subtle, and do quickly and lightly whatever it does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do what is necessary for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Some are formed in marriage, one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, up to fifteen, and all are fully formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious one.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	And it is necessary that the bailiff knows all this, for similar things happen by chance.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	This is a command, so the translation would be: Do as required.
de l’enfant mort	of a dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure a woman of a dead child or fetus, as I have said in the previous section, and it does not come forth naturally, and you are compelled to perform manual labor;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	It is necessary to know if the woman is of sound virtue, and not have any accident or fear of death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	The woman should be placed on her back, with her head inclined downwards, and her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	The minister should pull on the woman's hair by two handfuls, or tie her to the bed so she is not subjected to the delivery of the child.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then rub the husband's mouth with moist oil mixed with musk and fenugreek seeds and flaxseed, then anoint his hands with these oils and musks.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	Then push it gently into the socket, then hold one level or place where it pushes out the bones that are suitable for this purpose.
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take care if the tendons are not prepared that they do not stretch upwards on the head.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if you push the bones into his eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the wrist or near the sides,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the dislocation is on the limbs, push or press them to the midpoint of the ribs.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	And it is necessary that you press the opening with your right hand, and place the flat surface between its two sides with your left hand, and push gently with all your hand, and pierce the opening in any one of the places that we have said, until it comes to the hollow thing.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the opening:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then pierce it against another opening, or one that you have at hand, if necessary, so that the extraction is equal.
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	And then equalize it by moving from one side to the other, so that it may move out again; and the teeth should be clenched tightly to hold it in place, as shown in the figure.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if part remains, oil the hinges of some of his fingers with oil and push them into that part, and pull on the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if no part remains, place this finger or higher up, and do so until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be returned by the pulling,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then you must pull on a bandage until it is out.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	Then the heel in the joint of the foot or at the ankle, and similarly you must do in the other hand and with both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's hips are large and narrow in the birth canal, or if the head is pointed and assembled tightly,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	You must thrust the pointed spathulum between your teeth, and bend the handle and extract the juice.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	You shall grind it with the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the tools or chapter that follows this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	And in the same way, let the patient naturally expel it with great effort;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	And then draw out the bones with tweezers,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the shoulder joint jumps out and is held by force, it should be cut, as far as the moisture which is coming from within;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, strike it with hammers where you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the moisture goes away.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, it is a light attraction, and the direction towards the mouth of the womb is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is in the belly or feet, you must pull it out with one swaddled cloth on top of your hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and when the belly or feet have been corrected, it will come out.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	And if the other members are set bone, and the head remains,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	If the pincers should enter the wife's deepest part, and draw it out to the mouth of the wife.
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	Then put in one or two fingers, and pull forcefully;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the sore is narrowed due to hot abscess that has come upon it, one should not work on it.
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	then one must administer moist and fat substances.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and he applies plasters, and soothes in warm, softening, and moistening ointments.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the inflammation is on the side (costeit), and you can equalize it, then administer what was said earlier for a live child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if they do not have power over it, tear it apart into pieces and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done that, bring forth what we have said in abscess poultices that come in the marriage-box.  (This line is referring to medicinal poultices used for treating abscesses)
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And if bleeding comes forth, let it be stopped with sharp restriction, and bring forth other remedies. (This line is referring to stopping the bleeding with constricting force)
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman whose womb had been dead due to an infant being born, then another one was placed on top of it, and the death of the other was prevented.  (This line is referring to the survival of a second fetus after the first fetus died in the womb)
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came into the armpit, and swelled until it opened, and began to suppurate greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned for treatment, and for a long time, I could not heal the wound.   (Literal translation)
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong adhesive plaster, and an bone came out, and after some days another one did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly because the stomach has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I think it is the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I probe and touch the wound, finding several bones until the woman is in better condition;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman recovers for a long time in this manner, and then improves slightly by herself;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	And I have not heard of this chapter except that when the master finds an unknown thing, he knows how to treat it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the dislocated joint back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the pressor, by which books are weighed; and at two turns, the heads of the two links.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Moreover, the horns should be more subtle than the restraint, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the barrel should be one foot wide, and the branches of the tree one foot long, and half a palm in depth;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And between the two limbs should be two joints of the same bone, which are joined together firmly in one and the other, half a palm long or slightly more.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	And this pair of joints is inserted into the mouth of the wound when turning the two horns (or bones).
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made from ebony or boxwood, similar to the shape of pliers.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and say to the patient, as you see, two shoulders, two dislocations, of a palm's length, and two fingers' width.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see opening the woman with all the instruments, make her sit on one bed, her feet hanging and legs open.
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then push the two dislocations together in the woman, and hold the handle of the instrument underneath her thighs.
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then open your hand on the instrument, just like you did with the pliers, according to the amount that you see opening the mouth of the woman, until the bail makes her do what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is covered and multiplied in their similarity; and when the mirrors have arranged them, the work becomes more urgent, and higher for humans due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disperse the instrument unless you have arranged it, for its necessity cannot be excused.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must command the patient to hold her anus closed, and then make her vomit with cathartics, and hold her hands at the mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if it jumps due to this (cause), it is well (true).
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If it does not jump due to this (cause), then take a small pot and make a poultice or covering, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the sore, such as calendula, rue, anise, camomile, chamomile, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	Cook all these herbs or some of them in water over the fire; then place one end of the cloth or poultice from the pot into the mouth of the sore.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	And let the plaster remain until the vapors come within the marrow; then make it vomit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then immediately apply the second one.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment and does not heal as expected, command the maid to wet her left hand in oil of roses or musk of aloes, then put it on the affected area.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	Then find the second one; and when you have found it, take it and stretch it out straight, so that the marrow does not stick during extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	But it must be moved gently to the right and left, and then pulled out; if it comes and dislocates again.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	If the opening of the anus is stretched (or torn), we have said the treatment for evacuation and fumigation with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	If it does not have all the things that we have said, make sure you do not pull on it;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	But it is necessary that he who is at the mouth of the womb, you tie him to the woman's thigh, then anoint and clisterize with four-recipe ointment.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If it will open and return, and comes foul; however, when it becomes bad smell at the stomach and head, it bites the sick one.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is necessary to use suitable fumigation for this: no one has proved fumigation of dill and dried figs in the past.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flowers and the afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And is shaped like glass resembling a cane, with a thin neck in the middle, and wide openings over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And let the fumigation be on the coals and the taint until it is destroyed, and begin another one.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not yet pierced the foundation, but it has been stopped up by some subtle syrup.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore, in the bathing, it is necessary to pierce that syrup at its proper place, and do not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and be careful that it does not touch (the child).
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place a moistened linen cloth in wine and oil, then heal it with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not reform, then put or pierce a plaster of lead, and let it remain for many hours, and remove it when the wound appears to heal in rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this sudden swelling of wound or abscess comes; it must be covered. If it is healed, it should be treated with the lead plaster as we have said.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are swellings, and those that come out of the foundation are discharges, or in the gap between two parts,   (This is a loose translation of the original text, but captures the main meaning.)
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is a fistula or more than one; and when this swelling is old, it should be operated on, and then apply moisture to make it white or fine boils,    (This is a loose translation of the original text, but captures the main meaning.)
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And sometimes these fistulas are chronic; and they are known by those who attend them that there is either discharge or wind when the patient passes wind, and in some cases, it gushes out suddenly.   (This is a loose translation of the original text, but captures the main meaning.)
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it is fistulas that pierce up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; they reach up to the knee joint, and up to the navel of the cow.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And so one knows the fistula perforating at the bottom, and not piercing through it:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and is that you push your index finger or bottom, and insert a thin needle of ivory or iron into the fistula when it has no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	and if it has twisting, then insert a thin tube of lead, or horse hair, until you feel the tube or hair at your finger tip;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	And if you do not sense it, neither will there come pus discharge nor wind nor worm, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	Know that it does not pierce at all; hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is open up to the bladder or up to the channel of urine, if it gushes out urine and cannot be sealed with medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced up to the joint of the knee, if the tendon comes out at its place:   \n
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no twisting or the appearance of pain around it, then it is straight, and neither medicine nor salve will help it.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these Persian blisters, there is no cure other than work, and the futility of foolish doctors who meddle with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In those that are not Persian and are not ancient, in hopes of health through iron, as I have experienced,
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	And it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he lifts his legs up to his thighs, and bends his thighs towards his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then insert a tent of pitch (or a splint if there is a curvature), as long as you know where the tendon comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the foundation, then you must insert your index finger.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	If it feels as if the tendon has been pierced; and uncovered where you feel between your finger the skin or flesh, then know that it is torn.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If one does not work it at all, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One should always say that some can be well healed, but this is rare;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that one does, it is to heat the cautery delicately according to the width of the wound, as previously said.  ;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	And push everything hot into the fistula until it comes out from the base; and do this two or three times as you know that these charred things should be burned, which are similar to an eye-feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	Then cure the wounds with moistened tents in butter until the charred parts have healed, then cure it with a healing ointment made of char and resin.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is in such a state, that is good. Otherwise, it cannot be healed.   (The following sentence seems to be incomplete or missing some context, but I will still translate what has been provided.)
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	And if it tries to enter, and does not pierce as far as the base which is the foundation, and between your finger and the tent you put a thick covering of flesh or hide, and you see the fistula at the place where the covering was placed;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If the tip of the fistula begins to push forward against the tent, and then apply the cautery after, until it reaches the head of the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	The tent will be released and will break apart; then take out the fatty flesh that resembles a feather of a bird, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the limb goes away by itself, and breaks through [the skin], you shall cauterize it with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	The cautery of fire combines two good things: burning of charred wounds, and stopping the flow of blood and the removal of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then treat wet tents with butter or crushed cheese until the wound is healed and the charred areas are burned in the cheese.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat the wound with onions, hard charcoal, and dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	And when it is restored, it heals and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	If a fistula comes up to the full depth of the foundation and is removed from the body, push your finger or foundation into it, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tendon, and enter between two layers of fabric or leather or charcoal, where it is close to piercing, there should not be any obstruction except a way of faith and hope through one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	Or you cauterize it as we have said, or strike it to the bottom, or if you can, set traction and treat it as before;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And don't go too deep that you hit the holding element keeping the base, and let the swelling come out through its own will.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	Then heal it, as we have said.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	By chance, if it is purulent, remove that covering and clean it as soon as it is cut off at the base, either by force or by some other instrument pointed.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then boil the charcoal that is in the wound, as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then study to heal the wound and keep the fistula in the part away from the base; it will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes the fistula is of this type: and it is when you bite into the fistula, and it is on one side of the base beneath the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	If a tent made of pierced leather is taken on the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert one twisted thread into two, and push the tent with the whole length of the thread through the fistula as far as it reaches on the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced at the edge of the base within, then draw out the thread of that one, so that you push your finger or base.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	Pull the head of the thread and bring the two heads together, and bind one to the other, and leave it for one day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	And hold it without movement until the threads catch the charms that are between them, and burst.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound as long as it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst on its own, make it burst in all possible ways, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it should not be covered with a plaster if it is too deep, and then heal it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of a spur-like splinter from which a fistula is made is very sharp at one end and pointed;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and from the other side not, for that reason you should not strike where you should not strike, as you see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are within the foundation, like a drop of resin, and there are small and large ones, and on the outside there is blood,
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	And if there is one or more [dislocations], and they are dislodged from the foundation and the head of the foundation; however, those that are dislodged have little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and there is always some citron juice or a little blood, and they have the color of the body.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them within the foundation is that you command the patient to strain in order to urinate in chambers, until the foundation settles, and this appears in the sons.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you are in a hurry, hold it with pliers or grip it with your nail, then strike its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the pliers cannot hold it due to moisture, take a cloth or cotton, or a piece of leather;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and stretch them apart with your hands, then break and sprinkle some hot powders in their place as if for cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	Or you cauterize them as mentioned in the chapter of cautery, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot come out, then clisterize the patient with biting and sharp clisteria to clean that which is the foundation, so it can come out openly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	But if the patient is prepared and the thread is forced out from the foundation, then the treatment is easy.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And you should take them by your nail or tweezers, strike them, and then heal them as we have said, until they are healed and fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	The stitching should be carried out in this manner: take one twisted thread and put it on a needle, then draw the thread above and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is wide, form a knot with the thread, then tie the knot, draw out the needle, and do this for all of them, leaving one to let excess blood flow.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	Then place a soft cloth soaked in rose oil or balm on the foundation (or base), and place it on the affected area, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then leave it until it bleeds, and when it stops bleeding, treat the wound with ointment and other treatments, until it heals.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	the drying of the wounds or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often the drying of wounds occurs in the intestines due to natural constriction and when the disease is old and medicine no longer helps.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you pierce with a splint or your nail the bark above, so it does not become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal it until it is dry as needed;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot dry, repeat the shaving more strongly than before, until it heals and is barked.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let it heal completely.
dou fremit	great trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A louse is a small burrowing parasite on the body, and it goes very deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes the trout (louse) freezes, and it is felt as if one were dying from trembling, and it affects the entire body, but more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a cane made of goose feathers or a strong bird’s quill and put it on the trembling, until the purple circles surround the trembling completely;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand along the entire chain until you grasp everything around the limb, and place it in full, and pull the limb from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a chain made of iron or steel according to this form, and be careful beneath and pull above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce (it), to keep the tooth in place, and press it. And if you wish, cauterize the limb as described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of a clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At times, they make a silver or arsenic enema, or molten lead or mercury, and at times they make such small and large instruments, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, when it is used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and suffering, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema, whether it is large or small, should be above wide, or the belly should be bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	And it has an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the head pierced from one side by two wounds, and on the other one.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	And put medicine into the opening of the belly with a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierce it all around with small wounds.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And have one space between each wound, then fill in these wounds with strong thread of twisted thread in 10 or so (number) around, and sew up the belly like a goat's pouch.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And when the medicine is within, if it is tied to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then apply a plaster; and this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and smear the head with a plaster of oil or egg yolk, or similar, then place it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the ministers should press it with their two hands together until it is completely visible, then remove the plaster, and have the patient lift his legs to the open air.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	if the medicine appears, squeeze it as much as possible; and if it persists for an entire night, it is more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize it in case of disease of the intestines, and the medicine hastens to heal, keep applying it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	If the hemorrhoids are ulcerated or abscessed, then use as subtle a cautery as for an infant.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	This is the form of a subtle cautery where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division [section] the treatment of wounds; now we shall tell you the treatment for hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places or wounds where they are made, and from how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the thrust of a spear, cut by sword and knife, or lance or club or arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	What is done according to the body's laws, such as wounds that fall on the neck, or the head, or the side, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will start with the simple wounds of the head, for the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	When there is a simple wound on the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it comes from an arrow or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	And you doubt the opening of an abscess warmly: if it heals quickly from the head itself, even if blood comes from the wound, and healing is contrary to the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	And you fumigate the patient full of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	If it does not heal, reduce his food, and let him drink no wine, nor eat flesh;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	And place [something] over the wound, if an abscess comes up, put only cotton wool soaked in rose oil or in stiptic wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if there is no abscess, place [something] over the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood and not moving due to air or powder, I will say a little more about this later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is moving (infected), place some salves on it until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the size of a sword and cannot be closed with stitches, join them by sewing, as I will explain for abdominal wounds.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed of the bone, and gaping, and does not hold but only a little, close it; then heal the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Also instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as cooked heads and wheat, also as peas and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or cook meat putrefaction, and it is not to the bone, then cut off all of the putrid meat, throw away the pus, then heal.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, from which it cannot be stopped without cauterizing, then you must tie the artery if you find it dislocated with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy; it is that you put this powder on it so that the arrows have stuck.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the method of the powder is: take one part of incense, two parts of dragon's blood, four parts of quicklime, and pulverize it finely.  --> And the method for making the powder is to take one part of incense, mix in two parts of dragon's blood, and four parts of quicklime, then grind it into a fine powder.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	And apply the wound, and hold it open, until it dries well and joins completely with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And then bind it up well, and let it heal by itself, if it does not swell; for medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes they do this with just boiling water, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but the wound has not yet opened.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has already caused the wound to open, by all means do not apply this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	But place some digested onions or peas made from barley flour boiled and honey over it until it boils.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with fine tweezers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And I will tell you below about skull fractures.
de la plaie dou col	Of the collar wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes from the neck and it is simple, without a difference between it and the one on the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerve, there is no other remedy than to let it heal and not to put anything binding, for it harms the nerves and makes them shrink.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not place anything cold on the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	But the medicine should be boiled, as salt washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and also boiled again in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	And other stones of similar kind according to this method, and always moistened.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, tie it up with strips, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	If the wounds are deep and pus-filled, pierce or make a cut lower down;    --> "If the wounds are deep and full of pus, pierce or make a cut lower down;"
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the arteries are cut, bleeding comes forth, then tie it off, and lance it, and cauterization is needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the spine of the throat is cut or the windpipe severed, and the air passage is preserved, so that the meat goes to the lungs.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	If the windpipe is cut above the throat and not touched, but it is replaced according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then wait for healing, and let it rest for some days, then heal it with infusions of boiling herbs until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound presses against the bone, bind it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	If there are bone fragments, pull them all out if you can, and those that you cannot remove, leave until the wound heals.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	Make the exit incision straight and aligned.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wound is fresh, sprinkle it with the powder I have mentioned earlier.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of a wound from a lance or knife   (This line suggests that the text is discussing treatments for wounds inflicted by weapons.)
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, look carefully to see if air bubbles are coming out of the wound; because then the wound is deadly.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, but it is fresh with all its blood, do not put any powder on it immediately, nor tie it up so that the blood does not coagulate prematurely.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	And it returns to the heart, and kills the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but apply an attracting ointment, and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you have no ointment, place in the wound old cotton to draw out moisture,   and when the moisture is drawn out, leve les plaies ou il a estatz desespeses et desloiez, si com nos avons esproveit;
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	Make the patient sleep over the wound for 3 days or 4, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	If no spasm, no bad trembling of heart nor drawing of bowstring occurs.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good alignment, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat the illness and other treatments, as long as he is healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	And if it cannot heal, and an ulcer appears, immediately make sure there is a fistula; treat it as appropriate.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple (meaning not deep), or worse, or at the back, treat what is in front of it;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If the wound is large, sew it; if it is small, use powder; and if it has penetrated the bone and fractured pieces, treat the wound and draw out the fragments if they are dislocated.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if [the hairs] are not shaved, let [the wound] fester, align [the incisions].
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for other wounds on other limbs, the judgements are as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	Ruptures of the abdomen can be large, medium, and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From a large wound, the intestines occasionally protrude, or the nerves of the intestines, due to this, the insertion follows.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because one should put them in more carefully, if not from end to end.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines expand quickly when they feel the cold, so they should be put back in more carefully.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	And therefore, it is more important to treat the head injury, because you must move the intestines back into place for this one, rather than for the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	Know that the abdominal wound has four types:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The first two are common in the belly wound,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	And the belly wounds have common wounds of the body, and there are two more specific types for other wounds:
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And all of them are more appropriate with the suture on the stomach; I will explain one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	When the wound is small, and there is nothing from the intestines protruding out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	And there are two ways to treat it:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	For the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, heat it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Moisten a sponge or a piece of linen cloth in cold water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	boil it with squill and cypress and spikewood.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and remove the intestines until the inflammation subsides;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes you will make this wine restraining, and it should be matured until it becomes sour to dissolve.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see swelling parting, if you moisten the intestines with cold or hot and bad food,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for this closes the entrance to nearly nothing.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	if it cannot enter, then make a small wound with the instrument used for coping with piles.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	And the first treatment is cutting (the wound).
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	We should not cut it with great necessity unless necessary.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for cutting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	Cut through it in the hollow and do not deviate, observe its shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is widened, and the intestines leap out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	place it back in its natural form in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the ability, for it is worthwhile.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the abdominal area,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	It is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and raise their legs higher than their head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower abdomen part,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	If he sets the head and the foot higher than the parts below,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and similarly if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if he directs his intention to where the broken part should be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and in this way, it is necessary to apply what I say in large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Apply small wounds with what you have prepared.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then hold in your hands the emollient ointment that stains the entire wound with your hand.
et assemble les levres;	and apply pressure with lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common method of suturing wounds,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	And take an awl or more, according to the size of the wound's width.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	Leave from the top of the wound, i.e., two fingers' space, and insert an awl with one thread of strong wire.
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	Pierce the two shoulders with the two chies (a thin, pointed instrument) of the seifac (a leather-working tool or awl).
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierce through from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	And assemble the two chiefs of the hip, the four together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then pull on a double thread around the needle of two parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then assemble the two chiefs of the wound facing each other,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and leave one distance, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	Then tie the thread like you did the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing so according to what you need with the needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be medium, between fine and thick.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	Fine needles pierce through the entire flesh, and the large ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	because they should be medium-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and needles should not be pushed too deeply into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so as not to open and wound the flesh before the seam.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	And then cover the heads of the needles, so they do not prick the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and tie threads or cloths to the heads of the needles in order to hold them.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	leave it until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this stitching method with needles is more suitable for small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	For it pierces an awl or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and you assemble the two shoulders of leather and the two shoulders of sinew together with a needle that has one strong, thick thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced all four together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	If you reinsert the needle at the part where you began, in the manner as they customarily do with threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place a space between each stitch of the thickness of a hen's eggshell;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitching holds the man,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sew a wound that a man had or belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than one palm wide,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it exposed the intestines about two palms wide,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was within the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I returned the intestine as it had been twenty-four hours before.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewn up until fifteen days, and it healed, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not heal him with any treatment, because I was in one place where there was none, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And place old cotton above the wound twice a day, and wash it with honey water until it heals.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and push it from the outer part to within.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it has pierced the flesh straight through, place the knot or stitch where you put the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	And pierce through from the inside part until it protrudes on the other side.
