et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and understand this stitching that you sew in the same way as a tailor makes fur.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leave the seam allowance once on one side, then fold it back on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching that Galen calls
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	If one joins together, as naturally do, the two parts.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and applies one head of the knife to another head in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	inserts an awl or a head of a mirror-like instrument into that place only.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leaves the two heads of the knife.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	Then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part to that within.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	As two shoulder blades.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce one and the other from the outer part to that within, in two other shoulder blades that are opposite each other on the same side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the common way of stitching (or suturing) and the most common method.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen said this word, and no one testifies otherwise.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	you should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread in it.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one needle should be pushed from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew shoes.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	know that when the wound is in the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The stitching is more severe than other places on the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as those of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you touch the fresh wound with all its blood, in the same way as the herbs have moved it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you return the intestines and the coil; then place the powder of inciting charcoal on top.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	And if the arm has moved [it], place any available ointment on it until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and sew the thread, and bind the sutures, and apply the mummy [linen bandage].
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicine, place old cotton on it as soon as it begins to heal.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And move it twice a day while it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need any other medicine in various situations where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound spreads to the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	you should moisten light linen in warm oil or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And place it among the thighs, and beneath the buttocks;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	if there is pain or rottenness in the belly, and this happens many times,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if the clysterization of black wine is too hot, and especially if the rottenness reaches the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it perforates.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is because of the inflammation of the veins present there, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the close proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the worm jumps out of the wound, place it back in the same manner as the intestine while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	And if it is old and turned or black, then you must cauterize the black area where blood does not flow.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	For there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	Then, cut through the ligament (tendon or band of tissue that connects bones to each other).
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then hang the two shoulders below the wound area to align the extraction as the flesh falls, and press on the wound to keep it open.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are torn, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was pierced through the abdomen by a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	And the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and in it there was discharge and windiness.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it according to what I knew, and did not stop applying treatment until it healed and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw the wound closing, I feared that the patient might have pain in his abdomen;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	And there was no illness, but it remained in better conditions, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take large thistles, then bring together the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the thistles have opened their mouth, put it on the two lips.
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if it stretches its mouth upward;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then strike the head, and hold him so that he cannot dislocate.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another plaster after in that manner as before, until the wound is entirely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head becomes inflamed in the intestines, it brings no harm to the patient.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can bind the intestine with a thin thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal.
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestinal thread and make it very small.
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	And then tie the end of this thread (thread made of flax or linen yarn) to the head
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Thread the needle with the thread, sew the intestines and tie it at the wound site.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	This method of suturing wounds is not beyond faith and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great intestines, there is no tool nor health, but only skill.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or when it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	All wounds or abscesses that grow are universally called "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and likewise when it is healed and burst open again.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula, according to the truth, is a hard and white swelling where there is no pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And it is as hollow as a feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	sometimes clear jump bowed, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes thin, and other times quite;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	And I have spoken about it in the section on wounds, that any wound that is not healed and there is no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	This is not other than by one of the 8 causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	to wit, by the smallness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or by his ill-humor;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh within it, and above the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	There is too much swelling there.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	The joint is dislocated, and the matter is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	The medicine is not good in this treatment.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	because corruption is a manner of pestilence.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	For in the region [or area] it is slow the digestion, and slow the health, and it swells by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you the cure for fistula that is made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Note that fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from the large veins, and arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the stomach, or intestines, or bladder, or one of the ribs.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spine of the back, or any joint in the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And if it affects the property of the principal member and its corresponding joints.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all these fistulas are of great healing difficulty, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance in them.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not reach to the level I have mentioned, and you are confident in its cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you recognize it (the fistula), if you take a probe of iron or copper, if the fistula is straight, then pierce it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	And if the fistula is bent, search for it with a subtle probe of wood.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the probe bends due to the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has been crushed and you cannot search for it with probes.
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	cleanse the fistula with one of the crushed parts.
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	For moisture is cut from one place to another, and it is purified.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you should cautiously search for bones or nerves, and if it is completely closed,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press your hand there, and where the pain is located.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	And when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have said, if the head follows as I have said,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and cut open the falsehood and rotten cartilage that is inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then heal it until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	And if the fistula is properly opened in a straight direction, you must cut it through completely, as much as you can.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then you place moistened tents filled with healing medicine inside the fistula and push them up to its head.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the excess matter that remains at its bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then apply soothing ointments on clean wounds until they heal;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	And if they do not heal by this means, cauterize them as we have said;
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, crush it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves are not affected or the principal members (limbs), as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	And if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, let it remain until all the corruption is removed.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the adjacent flesh as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healthy, it should be made to swell as before.
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet at the fountain:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	If you uncover (or explore) and remain as deep as possible,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all corruption, then restore its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	If there is no other remedy but rest to nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can draw it with the pliers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction is possible with one instrument,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if there are many bones, take them all out, leave none of them.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	if the moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if it is soft, moist, and full of flesh, free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something stinking on the wound to encourage pus.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be purged around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then the bones will be more easily removed;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	And if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	then press the corruption only until the blackness is completely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of corruption that reaches down to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	If it needs to be cut (or cauterized) and covered completely up until corruption, then heal it until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to one man in his leg.
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	It was a young man of about thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	As long as substances came to the leg, and it swelled from a large abscess, without a reason for opening.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the people, by their foolishness, opened it so much that the abscesses burst open.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they corrupted a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and many pustules appeared that all collapsed and were wet with moisture in the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many people applied treatment for two years without any knowledge of healing in medicine.
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was called upon him, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and ran through the wounds with great speed.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the young man's chest became red, and had a yellowish complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I pitched a tent in one of the wounds, then searched for all the wounds,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	And I found that the veins come opposite each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	Then I hurried and made an incision in one of the wounds as far as I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	And I found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone within.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I appeared to be the bone corrupted, and I thought that there was no other corruption except for what I left.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And began to heal the wound with saline solution for a long time, but could not suture.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	Then I continued, and exposed the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And found the continuous corruption in the bone, and I removed it, then I tried to suture the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I cannot [do it] until I surround [the area] with a palm of the bone, and pull [it out] completely from its socket.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I will restore it with medicine; and it was quickly healed and solidified.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it no longer needs to be operated on except for the weakness of the patient, who could not withstand.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For due to evacuation it often bleeds profusely, but it was entirely healed.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and a hard cyst grew in the location of the bone, and it was well-placed and had no harm or adverse effect at all, neither in appearance nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, it must be treated as follows:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take one ligament and bind it around the open end of the broken bone,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	And command someone to extend it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another thicker thread of linen over the first one, and tie it above the flesh that is detached from the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	stretch the head so you pull the corrupt flesh downwards,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	expose the flesh in the place where it should be, so that the flesh does not cut the skin.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And place [something like] a splint or a board underneath the bone to cover the corrupt flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	It must be such that it can be seen and felt the corruption, and should also be checked again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupt but does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	If you uncover all the flesh; then place [something like] a splint under it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	And when the corruption spans from one part to another, and if the length of the corruption is a finger's breadth or more as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in a joint, then cut the corrupt joint and remove the bone from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, then it has no other remedy but to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is at the knuckle of the hand or foot, it is a very difficult matter,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	But in any case, it is necessary for you to investigate that corrosion, how it opens up;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve harm you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the saw and the files for covering these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and smallness, and their size and hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And because of this, it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each kind of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	And know that the work will show you the instrument that you need, according to knowledge in this craft.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimonies of the ways of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think about the instrument that is needed according to what is required.
dou feu	Hot iron
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder may dislocate from within or from outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have given this remedy, the corrosion by the cure of the medicines will not help.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	if it is necessary to cover that limb up to where the corrosion occurs,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	If the patient suffers from death by this means (cause), or by greater evil (malice), which is lack of a member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	And the signs are that the limb becomes black as if it were burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards the blackness spreads, then there follows the corrosion of member upon member.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and it takes hold of all the body; if you hurry to cover,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	And if it is caused by the strike of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corruption is in the neck of the toe, strike it but do not allow it to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, strike at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, strike at the edge; and if it passes the edge, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And no remedy of foreign substance is useful except for its quantity of power.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And thus do as when the corruption comes or falls: if it comes at the first joint, then apply the remedy after the next joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it falls down, cover the entire area with it.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, cover at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes upon the knee, there is no other remedy for the patient but to let him die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the method of treating or healing a limb is that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	extend a minister one of the lower bands, and another minister the upper band,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you draw out the flesh that is between the two bands, about one thumb-width wide, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then place or sew (the incision) with linen cloth on each side, so that the raw skin does not touch the healthy area.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And another wound and abscess come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And when bleeding comes during surgery, cauterize the area immediately.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you place some constricting powders on it; then return to your medicine until it is completed,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then bind the limb with a secure bandage and heal it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to a certain man in my town:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	There came upon him a blackness resembling burnt by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption first came upon his foot, until it took all of his foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the wound sees corruption, he pierces it with a copper lance and makes it heal.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	Long afterwards, corruption or decay came back to the wound or hand, and it came to me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I placed things that would stop the decay after the cleansing of the body, but the corruption could not cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to amputate his hand, and I did not want to, as I had hope of stopping the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	And he doubts that if I cut his hand, he will not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the virtue of the man was weak; and he gave up all hope, and returned to his earth.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and struck his hand with a sword, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I do not know this story except for the fact that they do it differently if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	An abscess sometimes comes to a charnut place, and stays for so long that it causes a large swelling of the bowel.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then bursts and pierces it, and makes the belly jump, and keeps the place open like a wound of a soldier.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin that is above is as thin as one layer of unbleached linen cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	And they shall not penetrate to the bone or to the nerve, and such illness is called "healthy."
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it reaches the bone in full, it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure is that you sew up the skin all around, and also when it is thin, just as a linen cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And it does not heal by its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	If you have faith that the skin heals, and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and if the skin is thick with fat, you should treat it with enemas like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look if the breasts are large, and the boil that is in it smells foul.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then, apply the Egyptian ointment medication that is made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take asafetida, oil, and litharge equally, put them to cook in one vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	And then take from these [things] according to your need, and make it [the mixture] into vinegar and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and anoint the breast, and press the sore;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by pulling;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this several times until the breast is purified and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	And at times it is clisterized with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take vine ash and pour water on it,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	Then cover it and let it be clisterized until you know that the wound is well healed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	if the patient cannot tolerate it, or the Egyptian medicine or water of ashes do not help,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	If the suppository is of water and honey, or it has a little crushed litharge;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you make the suppository of honey and sweet wine, where the honey has the properties of cleansing and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound heal.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	And when you have done this, and you have faith that the breasts are well cleaned,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the clustering of those who make it produce heat in them,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and you take a poultice made with linseed meal and oil and vinegar;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you clustered them with certain medicines and ointments, as I have said in the treatment of wounds;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	And if the boil on the breast is small and the probe of the cupping glass cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	with a small iron [tool] about a span long, and put an Egyptian plaster bandage on it,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and apply basilicon poultice when it is well spread out;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	And if the wound is too wide, let it contract and leave just enough space for a finger or a cloth to enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the ulcer that is boiling over is above, strike it or press it down below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the sore is deep, do not let flesh grow in it;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the chest beneath as you wish,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	If the shoulder bone aligns so that it moves to its lowest point.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the shoulder is fully set, do not leave anything in the wound
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you see fit,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	If the shoulder bone aligns so that it moves slightly downwards, and do not leave anything from the bone.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	And take consolidative medicines to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and place a linen cloth that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then apply force to the wound on the breast, which is slightly larger than the first one,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then anoint another cloth accordingly with the size of the wound,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	And place it on the pierced chest to align the bone, and do not remove the large bandage except after several days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and he who is on the pierced chest, frequently removes it in order to remove the bone.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	know what runs from the bone, whether it is poison or blood or digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	take care if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	And when your medicine is spread out in such a manner and you see the nature leap above the breast bone,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	know that the breasts have been pierced already, and approach the healing.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	then undress him in the morning or midday, and when you unbind the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	change one other bandage and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts sag due to indigestion after many days, know that they will not correct themselves.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisonous worms come after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health approaches. For there are men who have delayed healing in their wounds and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the breasts sag due to indigestion after many days, know that they will not correct themselves;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	And if the breasts are delayed in swelling, and they become hardened, apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in effect.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	As an ointment defined, for there is great part of vitriol, and it is the last remedy;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take the defined ointment, and make it with rose oil, and add equal parts of old wine in substance.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	Then cook it and use; and this very same thing cooked and fattened works better.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	When dew is absent,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them, and sprinkle the powder on the honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then wrap one piece of cloth around it, and place it on the breast, and at times administer an aristolochia root as a long-term medication,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And roots of this celestial plant, which is also like flour of vetch and centory.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simple or compound remedies: grind them, make into powder, mix with the honey I mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the patient is unwell, and this cure does not help him,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	Therefore, understand that corruption enters the joints and affects the bones or hard members, or ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If the treatment of a fistula (a tract or passage especially between two organs), as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of an abscess at the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or the foot, or by chance it arises in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes inflamed, and no attention is paid to it, a single abscess grows;
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and carve and grind bone until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance it may grind the entire thing;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And comes the corruption up to the bone, until pain smelling comes, and the shoulders are wide apart, and the color turns pale.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the section above, but the treatment does not help at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	If that does not help, then you must cut off any excessive growth from the nail.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is very great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is intact;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses against the flesh afterwards, and begins to swell, and suppurate,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	you must put the heated iron under the nail so as not to burn the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	And push upwards, and gently and lightly strike the flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and place on top of the remaining flesh, the remnant of the medicine that is burning and corrosive to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure with oil until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, strike and draw it out, as the more the bone is corrupted, the less likely it can heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the two parts broken, strike them together with a piece of bone as previously mentioned,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it until it is sound;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wounded, and swollen, and causes great pain, then it must be drained first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the tendon with a sharp scalpel across from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	And beware that the incision does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If it happens, place something on top to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The deafening pain of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	You should straighten the fingers that are born in some men's hands by chance, which are all fleshly.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	And sometimes there is bone or nail involved, and occasionally a fingernail.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Also, sometimes they grow in the root of the joint or in some of the fingers' nails.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	The one that grows in any nail of the finger does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	The one that grows at the joint of the finger may or may not move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The girth of one who is fatty is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	the girth at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	One who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: keep yourself covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or should be in the groin area, you must first cover the char roundly up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then bind the bone with an appropriate silk, then heal it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Simultaneously, swelling in the joints comes from birth, or from injury of the wound, or from burning by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you bind that swelling so that it can heal according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two wet linen or cloths soaked in rose oil so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	And you put between two thin wooden pieces, until the joints are soldered, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If one of its two (joints) comes with the palm, then strike that weld as necessary.
Des vils	Poor ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	These are large veins enveloped with mucus and filled with melancholic substances that come in many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it often happens with legs of those who walk and work and carry, more than with others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should sometimes administer purge of bile, and then heal the basilica (abdomen).
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron cure is in two ways: one is to strike them and draw out black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The third way is that you tie the vein and draw all the blood out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The length is as follows: first, raise the leg with hot strong water until the large vein becomes subtle.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then pull the patient's leg from above the calf to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then separate and draw the black blood from the vein to your hand, from one end to the other, as much vein as the illness can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then tie it up, and instruct him to bind himself with black sausage meat.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And repeat the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, it benefits the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevation is done in this way: lift the leg of the patient, if there is much hair on it.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Then put him in water, and raise the leg of the patient with warm water until it becomes swollen and the veins fill up.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if there is no swelling, heat it with fire, and then strike in the direction of the vein along the long part of the thigh or in the part beneath the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then open the skin with an awl and strip the vein from both sides, as far as it appears when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	It will appear red and black, and when it enters the skin, it resembles a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then push the bone back in place, as long as it is swollen with skin, and then bend it gently at the angle.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then strike the bone in another place three fingers away; then cut the skin over the vein as far as it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then tie the bone again, as you have done, and bend it to another angle, as you did before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then strike another shape, or more if needed, then tie it, and bend it to the second knuckle of the finger.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then draw and drain up to the second rib; then remove it rib by rib until it protrudes entirely, then break it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw and drain, push an awl with a very strong double thread through it.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and draw it out, then push under one rib, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it protrudes.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not break, because if it breaks, you cannot draw or lift it out, and it harms the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it completely, place wool soaked in vinegar and oil on the wound site; keep treating it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	If the wound is contracted, twisted, and rolled together all at once, and it's not straight as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If it needs to be cut, it should be cut twisted but not covered; follow what we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron used to strike the vein is curved, but does not cut, it should not pierce the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is large in curve, for if it is fine, it would pierce the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the form:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in warm areas where no grass or trees grow and on dry ground.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And sometimes it arises elsewhere than in legs, and this happens because of corruption that comes beneath the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as snakes come within the body, worms attack between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great inflammation comes in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then the vein changes its course, and the flow of blood begins to exit, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the shoulder is dislocated open, you should wrap around it a piece of wood from 1 to 1 and a half feet long, and sew it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	leave the wood in place at the leg, and every time it slips out of joint, re-wrap around the wood and sew.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	if it is too long, cut off a part of it and re-wrap the remaining, but do not cover its root until it has all come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut off [the wood], it goes back into the flesh and causes an abscess or inflammation and bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For that thing it is necessary that it should be treated little by little until the head, and no remainder should remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein when it is treated is five fingers long or ten,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	And one man came to me, from which it was ten fingers long, and when you cut it, it gushes out a pint or more, and pierces through to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	So that everything inside it empties out; and let the matter within be voided, and for three days bring in medicines that promote healing to the place, then treat it as an abscess would be treated.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes at this vein many hands are used, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or hand.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and a great deal of bleeding occurs, and it jumps out; treat it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called on our land "cattle disease," because it often happens to cows.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, which moves throughout the body expanding and contracting.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it feels pain in one limb after another, until it pierces through the skin where it is going, and jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is infected by corruption of certain humors, such as worms, snakes, lice and roundworms or the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And one doubts its nature, because when it goes through the body, and reaches the head, and comes to the eye;
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	sometimes enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you want to treat it and draw it out, one cannot avoid it but when it goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	Therefore, you must tie the joint above and below with a strong cord tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then pull on it upwards and straighten it out fully in the flesh, and do not twist it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If you burn with fire above, let it die.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm it does is to run oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the oil, hold under it the bellows shaped object, then strike above and pull it off;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	it is necessary to use the patient with purification of the body with dissolving medicines for bad humors to pass.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and let the patient eat boiled meat without seasonings or sauces.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and it moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I will tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and when I examined her arm, I saw a small swelling in the armpit.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And, as if a worm, the eyes should rise to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than anything, as living silver when it cuts from one to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain is divided from that place and pierces in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little after it runs through the whole body, until it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she turned back again around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many cases where pain moves from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen this before, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	And I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins uncovered.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason that condition appears constricted.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	but it does not appear in accordance with this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and veins closed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you wish to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If the ligament above and below is tightly stretched, then press on top until the swelling returns to its place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the joint; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if you treat those who swell up with drugs such as fetid pills and serapin pills, and similar ones.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity among them is that some have large points, small, sharp and blunt ones.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two points, those with tongues, and those with splinters.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and a dislocation of any member occurs in two ways: either in the principal member, which is the head.
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the member that includes the brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it occurs in any location of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	It is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death follows in many cases.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if this ill sign does not appear at all, and the arrow is not fully in, pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when an arrow pierces the bone and exits above it,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It is concerning cataract, stone, and gravel in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it may lack force from the nostrils, or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps from the wound white matter similar to pus, and also as bruise of flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears, take care of the treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is not within.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of an arrow when it strikes or pierces is that it is close to the left breast, and it feels like it has been driven into a hard object, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	Furthermore, the arrow may become quiet like hair and produce black blood, and bring coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, it is clear that death is at hand.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that penetrates the flesh deeply is when there is no scum discharge from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, breathes heavily and seeks a warm place.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the cover of the mattress, it should be removed through the small openings; and you must release great pain and great suffering and groans; and all the members of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, by chance, something of indigestible meat may jump out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly or abdomen, and does not jump out through the intestinal route, there is no hope in the cure nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and loin and hips and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it does not move, as I will tell you what happened to me, for this reason that you do the following:
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man that an arrow or splinter lodged in the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to extract it from below the fat of the ear, and found no sense (meaning nothing but pus).
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And extracted with play a splinter that lodged in the fat of the eye beneath the paper.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the splinter was turned, but could not reach the tip towards out (meaning it had curved back upon itself).
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, and it could easily pierce ears; the wound was clean, and no bad accident happened to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And pierced an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and the arrow had ears (like a crossbow bolt):
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was the barber, and made it thin enough that I pierced it, and the Christian was unharmed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And pierced an arrow through one man, who was either head or belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And since it has passed more than thirty days, its position does not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut across the arrowhead, trapped it, and pulled it out without any adverse effects.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you want to wound one man with an arrow who is on his back, and the wound has been sewn up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And the arrow remained inside, and it did not cause any change to its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	It finds no harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And another man, who had an arrow shot into his body, and the wound was stitched up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and endured like that without suffering great pain; and many similar things happened.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And through an arrow struck one of the prince's men who had fallen into the ditch,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	And it was slightly sloping to the right side; and the arrowhead was fully lodged.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned to treat her after she had fallen for three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I felt it all with a thin probe, and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and it felt tender and pain beneath her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the point of the arrowhead
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed the attractive and digestive plaster on the affected joint, as the joints should not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and it appeared to be from the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the plaster for many hours, and directly healed the wound, and the patient stayed well for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	As long as he feels the arrowhead inside his neck for a day; then he tells you [about it].
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I apply the wound with corrosive medication by hand for several days until it is cured.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I try, and feel the tip of the arrowhead sticking to the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I apply an incision to the wound with that corrosive medication until the arrowhead appears visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	And passed beyond the limits within 4 months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	Then uncover the wound that I pierced with the pincers, and pull it apart from both sides, and could not extract it.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I continued to refine and invent means of instruments until I took it with well-made pincers after 1 hour.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	In accordance with what its form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I hold it and return the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the mirror judges that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	Then I will restore it, and the wound will heal, and the patient will be completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	I have told you about the qualities of extracting some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	If you apply your care to this which I do not entirely specify, for books cannot fully grasp it;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters understand a little of what is happening and concerning the present and failing condition,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	they perform nine works and nine operations, below the remedy of things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not enter members where they are driven except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the side where they enter, or from another direction;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out from there where it enters, it is an arrow entering into the flesh, and it may jump out at times now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh heals around it and align the opening.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And in the same way, if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps (or moves), and if it does not jump, pierce it all around with a small needle, as long as the surrounding area is widened, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	If the arrow is inserted into the bone of the head and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And some of the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: do not pull it at all, but let it remain even after several days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow reaches there (its target), it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	But if the arrow has not penetrated all the way, and does not reach its target,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	The patient remains for some days without serious complication, if the extraction is properly handled.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it (the arrow) is deeply embedded and cannot be removed, administer tourniquets around it as I told you, then heal the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is put back into its place within the body but cannot be seen, try to find it thoroughly.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, take any suitable instrument and draw it out;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if the wound is too narrow or the arrow too deep,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if there is no bone or nerve or vein, widen the wound as much as possible;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	And draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on the arrow like it grips,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	and push out the bone that is stuck in two parts where you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as much as you can pull it out.
