et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	be careful that you do not break the arrow, but rather pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot dislocate it once, push the leg towards the joint, then draw it, for extraction will be easier in this case.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding makes disobedience to you, bring what we have said about the cure in its chapter:
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting the nerve and vein, and use an instrument as you can draw out the arrow safely,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; place the patient according to the shape that he was when the arrow hit him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For it is the greatest help that there can be, and if you cannot do this, set it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, opens something of it, or the skin is swollen in that place as one can see or feel apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut therefore above, as long as the scissors can take it, and then pull it out; if it does not come out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone, widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	If it cannot come out, leave it still and then continue the extraction until it comes out completely;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it were from the arrow shaft, push it all the way in;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it fell out, and you wish to administer medication, then administer one medicinal instrument.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	If the tip of the arrow enters into the hair of the weapon; then push force.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is stuck in the hair, push the instrument with its point entering in.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touched, you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if an arrow falls or pierces the belly, bladder, side, and it is close by, and you can cover it, then do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	But be careful not to pierce the vein or nerve, and then remove it, and then stitch the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and nurse it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers used to remove arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The form of the hairy growth is also like the feather of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to pierce the tip of the arrow, as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tweezers for pushing and testing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The number of veins for purging are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen main ones.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	It is to be known: 2 bands which are after the ears, called the double "herbich";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the 2 arteries that are in the 2 temples visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the 2 veins that are in the 2 eyelids of the 2 eyes, called "aspirers";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein which is on the forehead; and the vein which is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two tendons which are at the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two tendons above the mouth, and these tendons are called "augheherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two tendons beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The tendons that are commonly known as five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the chest, and the common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called "fistula", and consists of both the cephalic and basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side of the chest.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the liver.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and this is the one which opens clearly above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the veinlet is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two [branches].
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and foot there are four veins: one is under the shinbone of the left thigh,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second saphenous vein that is on the right shin, and the vein called "nese," which is in the left shin.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are four veins beneath these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The venesections that follow the ears help with ancient catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of a surgeon, as I tell you, is that you seize the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins or vein is with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Draw your fingers to your throat, and where you feel the pulse beneath your throat, press firmly.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance, thrust it under the vein until you reach the bone, and draw your hand all along the vein upward.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut through the skin and the vein about two fingerbreadths deep, and make the blood come out until you see it.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then tie and let it heal completely.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The draining of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is worth emigrating an old man.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and softening, and otalgia accustomed, and to the heart of the eyes with hot water;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of draining are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is instructed to the patient to stretch out his neck, until both veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse beneath your jaw, and then press hard;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the heel of the finger above the vein at the jaw, and push the needle in beneath it;
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	lift up the vein and squeeze it, just as you have done with the other two veins, and make a hole according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then tie the patient, and put your hand on the vein for an hour, then cover with cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then let it heal, until it is healed; and we have spoken about their covering and their extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the healing of the skull in ancient facial diseases, and migraines, and fevers.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its qualities are such that the patient twists his neck to make the vein appear.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and press from above with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the amount that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then cut off the patient's neck and tie the vein until it is dry and not used once with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Moreover, the flames should not be too sharp; and slice across as the bone is near, so that the flames do not break when they are thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The salve of the two veins that are in the armpits helps the eyes, and the swelling, and the redness, and the ulcer in oil, and the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of its salve are that the patient stretches his neck by twisting with some rope, as mentioned before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then put the salve on it, and let the salve be of the cross, a little long and wide, for there is no heat in it.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, they may break [the patient's skin]; then make a wound of blood, as much as you need, and then cover it with linen, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The vein of the neck is useful against ague, and against smallpox, and diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as migraines and redness that come on the face, especially when they are old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the vein is that the patient squeezes his neck, then you press your left hand on his neck,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	And take the subtle flame long, and thrust it between the two nostrils.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well in that place, and the pus will soon begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then leave it for a night, for it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the form of fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The salve of two kinds of gundeges aids in the setting of a fracture, and at the beginning of mesh-work, and much in diseases, and in stopping abscesses, and in corroding, and in herpes, and stomach ulcers;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the salve is that the patient stretches his neck over one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and the master standing on top of the patient's head, and the patient lies on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then open the vein along its length widely, then draw out the blood moderately, as needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then fix another part in the other vein, then tie the ligature, and hold all the veins moderately tight,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	On Curing Rabbits
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The purification of veins in the mouth above helps to cool [the mouth] and promotes decay of the gums, fissures in the lips, toothache, and surrounding areas.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of this purification are for you to seat the patient before you and hold their neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And they are recognized by being black, and by the small black veins around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Take both of them then, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt.
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if you take the larger one from each side, and also do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same way.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The evacuation of veins located beneath the tongue assists after the cephalic vein has been opened, and it is at the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the bloodletting are that the patient lies supine before the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks under each side to find a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then, let one of them be taken, and do not go too deep, as beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the cost, which are commonly healed according to two ways, are as follows:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or when pricking with all fire, either mirrhin large or subtle olive oil as you use to cauterize, and it is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are broad and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirrhine is very renowned, and it is wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it should be used to open the veins with large arterial blood appearing, and those that contain large blood and turbulence;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is pointed more subtle, and it is for treating subtle veins that contain subtle, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The sacred vein of the basilica, one of these veins, assists in treating illnesses located below the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the patient to drain pus profusely and urinate from the artery that lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	If it pierces the artery and bleeding occurs, then it must be stopped, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And should not be poked with a flame, but rather cut like scissors.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, you must dislocate it and change another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	If the artery is blocked, or if the vein does not open when cutting into the arm, it opens manifestly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and heat the iron in the fire as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	If you want to discover the location of the artery, then it is necessary to dislocate the arm and touch the place where you can feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the joint with a sign, then bind the arm, and heat the vein with fire.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And watch that you do not cut into the artery when you see the joint swollen, for it is of the artery; then avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rising high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is not from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Then hurry up, place your thumb on top for a long time, then remove your thumb if the blood stops flowing, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Keep the arm still, and let it be so, the patient does not move it; be afraid and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the artery does not appear swollen and it inflames, and there is no medicine present, cut open the artery if it is open, as the head of the wound recedes; bleed the limb.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of willow bark, cut it in half and place it on top until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the limb is not bleeding, that's good; if not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And cauterization is not always appropriate in various positions due to the small size of the wound and the thickness of the ligament in the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein-letting in the middle helps to remove blood from the head above, and from the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And the lord must pierce it through the nerve that is below, and if it pricks too deep and strikes the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it inflames and the wound becomes painful and perhaps cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens frequently, and if it does not open in any men due to its subtlety, then you must open it with the instrument anesthetic; and cut off the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The sanitary aid for the head helps, as it draws blood from the head, and assists the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to sanitize when pricking with olive oil or myrtle flame, for it is the safest of all veins, for there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Moreover, it is necessary to seek the more delicate place and not to hurt anything when it needs to be done for the first time, and then repeat.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And sometimes the joints swell in some men, what should be done for the first time, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the urine is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about urinating is that urination is not brought forth except for the purpose of maintaining health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	Let the vein be opened in one of the four veins that are named: cephalic, femoral, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	It should be done to open the vein at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of swelling appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	It should be done to open the vein on the first or third day, after two or four hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The treatment for illnesses has no set time, but when there is need at day or night, in every hour and all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	It is not necessary to treat children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman in labor except during the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	One should not treat the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wishes to be treated in any way, it is necessary that the intestines be cleansed with a light clyster.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If many worms are retained, so that the veins do not expel the waste products into the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor heal the one who is excessively salted with meats, or drunk, so much that he vomits, or watery.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if he is purged after colic, vomiting, abdominal distension, excessive sexual activity, labor, vigilance, and fasting, and his strength or from the weapon or the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then refine the bodily fluids, if they are thick, with foods, drinks and medications, if you have the power to do so.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then enter or use a bath, if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal the vein with the sickness around the third part, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep yourself from labor, pain, lust, and similar things on that day.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And bind and press, and let the bandages be higher than the one being treated, and rub the arm twice or thrice.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then gently pull the ligature upward in a moderate manner, for if it is too tight or too loose, it cannot heal without.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell, and feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then dip the bandages in a little oil, and place your right thumb on that vein under the area to be treated.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	The vein should not burst when opening it with a knife.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that behave like cords in drawing, and some are filled with wind,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if one puts fire above it, when withdrawing the flame, it cannot open the vein, and thus is the case with some.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	If the vein opens, the wound is too narrow, so the surgeon must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If the vein opens again later or too quickly, and the wound is not inflamed:
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	If the wound is inflamed and the patient fears it, allow him to rest for one or two days and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	If pus comes, do not enter it into the wound and do not bathe, then wait for the wound to heal before starting again.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the wound is small or shallow, and you doubt that much blood will flow from it, you should cauterize the wound with direct flame itself.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	Perform a little more vigorously, so that the flesh is inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the flesh inflamed, do not start bleeding again, and put a little oil on it, because it will cool down the blood, and the oil is made in this place.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And administer the oil in each bleeding that you perform to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And the same thing happens with triangles and bows when put back in place; if they are too delicate or split when they are too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes large abscesses, which happens frequently, especially when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	Press quickly and place the moist sponge in hot vinegar and hold for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary that you do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after several days without any blackness or greenness, it will not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh beneath a hot compress, poultice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and appearance occur at the base of the basilica; place your hand on it then, if you find it soft to the pressure of the hand, this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then be careful not to apply anything mentioned above, for by chance it is in court without the artery; but let it have one dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another medicine until it heals and becomes healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood according to its quantity based on its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it turns red; and if you see it swollen, let it drain until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is full and hollow, and requires extraction of blood, to make a larger wound, and let the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to let blood drop by drops and often, and it should be done by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this way of bleeding is free from the danger of blood clotting and nerve damage, and is more useful than bleeding by length or width.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body needs to be bled, it is necessary to give soft bread soaked in grape juice; if he is chilled, bleed him four or five times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of cold complexion, let him eat before the sweet bread soaked in syrup sweetened with honey or scented honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and anise, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if it swells after the discharge of blood, then let him drink broth of meat and fragrant subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things as we have said in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if you want to fracture some bone, and heal it again as needed, when it is weakened by excessive healing, it should heal little by little, according to the quantity of its power continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if you want to fracture some bone after the first healing, and it has strong flesh, it heals seven hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if you want to heal from another part, it should heal on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood within the body which has been heated, and it causes fever; therefore, it requires drawing a large quantity, and opening the wound until it gushes out.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you apply all the signs of healing and place your hand over some pulses when it heals, so that death does not come in its place.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	And this happens many times when healers are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not good when you dislocate the arm and cause bleeding a second time, and the wounds are closed, that you press forcefully.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is curved, do not stretch out the arm abruptly, for it would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it until the bleeding stops a second time; or you prick it with the tip of the flame, so that the frozen blood from the vein flows out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place one piece of fresh linen dipped in vinegar on top, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is burst, leave it and do not squeeze it until the abscess has been soothed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the necessity arises to draw blood a second time, do it in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are healthier than the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method for drawing blood is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the vein becomes red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then tie it moderately, so that the vein appears well, then hold it steadily from one side, not wide nor long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the wounds be opened widely, and press well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be drawn out, put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is in summer, do not put the hand in hot water, because you are putting it more into winter than summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the vein of this vessel is safer than all other vessels, for there are no artery or nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The swelling of the hand on the right side is worth all liver diseases, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is emptied, if one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the wound is transverse, and you cover it entirely, it will not cause any harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	Do not go too deep, for the nerves are beneath all exposed without flesh.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then put the hand in hot water, if the wound is frozen, it will not thaw.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as much as necessary, put oil and linen over the wound to bind it quickly, and do this with each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purgative of the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do as I have told you regarding the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The poultice from the sow's belly is good for all diseases that are beneath the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as the illness of the anus, and retention of flowers, and disease of the loins, and knees and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of its purgative are that the patient puts their foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it breaks.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And he lies above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, it goes very deep.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Cut open then a larger vein, or at the ankle, which is more effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut open above the foot, guard against the nerves that are beneath, and cut through as well as possible like in cutting; let the flames be still.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the bone cannot come out, place the foot in water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is necessary to clean the first time, start the second time a little above, because the wound is salted.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same for the other side equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The wound of the sciatic nerve is at the knee joint, and its cleaning relieves pain in the ankle, when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its cleaning is that the patient immerses themselves in water up to the knee joint while twisting it four times.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	Otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, drain it in all possible ways that you can, and by crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	Moreover, you should cover it because the wound is hollow and it is greatly swollen in the hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not treat it, no remedy of any kind will open or close the wound or stop the flow of blood.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and let the wound heal as you see fit, then untie the ligature, place cotton on it and press down; the wound is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Drainage from a blister
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Corns or hair, or glass are used for blistering, and blistering is done in two ways: either by making an incision to draw blood, or without making an incision.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	This blistering without making an incision is done in two ways: either it is done with fire or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and the blistering that is made by making an incision and drawing blood is done in twelve layers of the body.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	The one is completely asleep with his head; The other is in a neck position.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on both sides of the neck; and the abscesses under the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the abscesses on both shoulders; and the abscesses above the ankles.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and abscesses in both arms; and abscesses in both legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the boils of the two shins; and boils do not bleed, unless from small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason, you should not drain them at all, as is done with bloodletting from veins;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered in any case, neither with hot nor cold water, in any illness that comes from accumulation, until the entire body is purged.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	If it is necessary for the treatment of illnesses to perform bloodletting, or due to custom, we will administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the morning and evening.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to fart, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and to those who find repletion and redness in their abdomen, their head, and neck, and blindness of the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, have swollen tongue, and bleed;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are some who faint, see blood in their urine and nosebleed, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially if it is in the month, we order to ventose after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The purging of the nose helps the inflammation of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the whole body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this purging is instead of the purging of the head,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	it should not be used by those with cold constitution or who have catarrh, as it does great harm to them.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore, it is not advisable for those who have cold heads or sicknesses to use [the cautery].
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves become negligent, and for this reason, the cupping glass should be placed a little lower due to the fear of negligence.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The cupping at the neck is in the position for the healing of the head and the basilica, and therefore it is beneficial for the treatment of the spine.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	And to cut through the channel of the thighbone, and completely, and to fill.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	It should be slightly pushed as if it is too tightly closed, it may cause obstruction in the intestines or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The windings in the two ribs of the neck are equal to headaches, and ear pain and migraines, and strangulation, and toothache at the roots.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it should be in the place of the wound in the basilica; and you must instruct the lord to extend his hand to make the incision, so that he does not cut the artery, and no bleeding occurs.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilations under the chin are useful for mouth diseases and gum decay, as well as other mouth illnesses; they should be placed in the locations of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilations under the armpits are useful for diseases that originate from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventosations of the costal joints are worth as much as three veins of the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the lord not to enter too deep, for the flesh is bare there, and it knows of nerves and arteries below.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventose on the buttocks is worth as many emorroids from the bottom and diseases below, and it must be large, and made of metal, for it needs to draw well; and in case it is too thin, it will break; and it will cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings in the legs open widely, because they attract blood from all over the body; they are similar to ancient rain sores, scrofula (neck swelling) and bladder stones; they weaken the body after a long time, and bring pus into various conditions. They are located in the area of the knee joints and ankles.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of treating the swelling is to first empty it, suck it quickly, press it evenly, and continue doing so until you see the area turning red and inflamed, and the redness of blood appears; then stop, and place the swellings, and take care in the disposition of the body, because there are some who have thin skin and clear pores: if this is the case, it should be cut once only, and the wounds should be large and deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the skin is thick, it should be cut twice: the first time to make the way for thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the wound is very thick, it should be cut three times; and when we want to draw blood drop by drop, we should only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want much blood, we should prick often; and if the wound is thick, we should pierce completely, and ensure that the veins are pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and with narrow pores, to anoint the joints of the wounds with penetrative and soluble oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of cucumber seeds.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in fever, of oil of watercress, or lilies, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one that is to be healed has tender flesh and wide pores, no oil should be applied.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it should be washed after the fumigation with rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise from bed with the aid of aspen wood, or water of myrtle, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And he who has large excesses should rise with old wine or juice of sourdock, or a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and one should not bleed with a veinlet before the bath or during the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after venesection.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he urinate when he needs to bleed and after bleeding.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And observe that the patient who is healing is colicky, and if he lacks bile and becomes excessively heated.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	then it is necessary for him to take cold things, such as pomegranates and endive and lettuce leaves, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat little, consume pork meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And the one with a cold constitution should take honey syrup and fragrant wine that is neither too old nor too new, and eat sparingly, consume pork meat, and small birds and songbirds.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day when it swells, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And sometimes one should give a man triacet or muscat to strengthen the main limbs before or after swelling.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And the wine must be refined but it is not suitable for those who are hot-tempered to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The swellings that are applied to wounds are those placed on the liver, the spleen, gout, abdomen, flank, and groin, because these members cannot tolerate being wounded there.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	And let it not be done unless to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we put on the limbs when the tumor is in a member; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put leeches on the abdomen and the buttock to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain when there is an obstruction or arrow, it removes by its virtue attracting the obstruction or draws the arrow out of its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it does when placed on the liver and the spleen where there is retained wind.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these blisters are treated empty for suction only; sometimes they are treated with fire, and at other times filled with cold water,
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as with diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a manner the bladder is filled with hot water or water that has been boiled with herbs appropriate for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the bladder treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be two fingers in width and half a palm of breadth, and have one small hole on the middle side, as when pushing an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and be of iron, soft before so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	have in the middle a rod of iron or steel, to insert a handle;
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And they may be large or small according to the diseases and age of those who contract them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the boils of children are different from those of adults, and the thin ones from the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And this boil should be placed over the member like so:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take a stick of candle wax or linen thread and place it through the boil across the length that is in the boil,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	"The light should be deep within the bladder so as not to burn the patient."
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	"And then place it over the member, and your fingers should be over the puncture that we mentioned, so that when you look at it, if steam goes out, remove the bladder."
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	"Wrap it with linen in the same way as before, and repeat as necessary if required."
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	"In the bladder used in case of pleurisy (a disease of the lungs), there should be no needle or puncture. It should only be placed over the member when it is full of fluid."
et c’est li forme:	And this is the shape: [The original text does not provide a shape; it seems to be a statement about the subject matter.]
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Incisions are not made in places except for members where one cannot put leeches due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in bare flesh areas like the palm of the hand or fingertips, and other similar areas;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the quality of using leeches is that when you find ones that are in sweet clean water without poison, you should take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And place them in a warm, gentle poultice until they are familiarized (accustomed) and have no growths in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	Then let them be purged with veins and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red and apply leeches.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	When they become full and warm, if a vein can be applied or cupping, do so, for it is of great benefit.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If there is no vein to apply or cupping, raise the limb on a pillow, then immerse it in warm water, and then cover it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the joint becomes too swollen after the body, immerse a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the swelling subsides;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the wound becomes multiply, apply ground glass (vitriol) or similar things until it dries up.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or apply half of the beans peeled to the wound and leave it until they adhere to the wound, it will dry up now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the veins do not want to be taken, rub the place of fresh blood, or insert a needle until the vein bursts.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	then tie them up and as soon as they feel the blood, they coagulate.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are bleeding, sprinkle some powder of aloe and crushed seeds or ashes, then they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear child, that the fool-sick man should fall from this chapter, he never saw any ancient books, nor did he read a single letter of it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, the science is estranged in our land, for I never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing about it except through the science of ancient books that I have studied for so long that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought in, just as I have done in these 2 chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us say the summary of this book, the number of words and chapters where the wise put their understanding and dwell on truth, so that those who have been proven knowledgeable will know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or distortion comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to clean the wound from both sides, unless something prevents you, such as weakness of the body, infancy, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the time is not very hot or too cold; and eats cold meat, meaning cold meats, and poultry and veal, and does not drink wine, nor eats any fattened flesh, and does not fill himself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you doubt an abscess is hot, or spreading of matter in the limb; then the patient returns to their first rule as they have used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with foods that make large stools, or they have thick consistency, such as cooked wheat in water, and peas, and heads, and feet, and pork belly, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this nourishment brings on softened stools and the broken bones heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of the old and weak cannot be well retrieved nor joined according to their nature due to the relaxation of members, neither those who are too soft, as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but has no cure, set above the broken bone.i.e., large strong splints that support and join the member together, as it was before; and do not let it at all from its work, and for this reason it should be fed with coarse foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the breaks are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the neck is different from the break of the foot, or the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of break.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There is a break that grows over time, and another that sharpens, like the quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a break with a wound, and a break with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type has its tool, and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory comes to its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that bone fractures occur when the bones are twisted, broken open widely and splintered under pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And if there is no twisting or touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can have twisting, a break, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand, but apply medications that follow, and then hold it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks that go to the armpit, and are the two parts disjointed, you must now put them in an even position, thus allowing abscesses to heal.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses come, leave it for any day, until the abscess is calm.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it in the same position as you can easily and skillfully, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration where there are pieces; then press, as needed hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces and it breaks in two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or if your hand breaks one of the smaller members, or two cords, or one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	align the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are dislocated, you gather back all additions in their original place using whatever means you can, and make sure your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	align well the two joints of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you should feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: straighten it out nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring it forth by their work abscess heat and contraction to the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	When the limb is well set, punish the patient so that he does not move it, neither while watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And carefully ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	When it feels no pain, it is not dislocated, and it should be placed in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And keep it straight so twisting does not come when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are various in smallness and largeness and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers: it is necessary to wrap them in linen cloths soft and fine;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and hard bandage, for the broad bandages embrace the entire large limb evenly, pressing it from all sides equally, so that there is no swelling;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then bind light padding around it, 3 or 4 turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little on the bandage, then go above the fracture and tighten less, than the fracture, then move away from the fracture.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the ligament bit by bit, until you take a large part of the healthy limb, then take another ligament and turn it around backwards over the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the part below the break and hold it gently, neither too strongly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first lesson above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the ligaments pads of linen or cloth, until they are all even, then tie everything above with one bandage, and then place well-made stirrups on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something soothing on the abscess and let the one who removes it wait for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then tighten your legs, and they should be half as thick as a large cane, tightly bound, or with ropes used for splitting logs, or with palm branches, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but the bandage that one places on the break should be slightly larger and thicker than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And let it be as long as necessary for the member, whether of small or large size.
